<script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">
  function buildMathJaxPlaceholder(width) {
    const placeholder = document.createElement('div');
    placeholder.setAttribute('style', `width: ${width}px; height: 0; font-size: 1px;`);
    placeholder.setAttribute('class', 'math-tex-placeholder');
    placeholder.innerHTML = '\\[\\]';
    return placeholder;
  }

  function expandChildren(element, parentSelector, childSelector) {
    element.querySelectorAll(parentSelector).forEach((el) => {
      el.style.width = '100%'
      el.querySelectorAll(childSelector).forEach((el) => {
        el.style.width = '100%'
        el.style.display = 'block'
      })
    })
  }

  function contractChildren(element, parentSelector, childSelector) {
    element.querySelectorAll(parentSelector).forEach((el) => {
      el.style.width = null
      el.querySelectorAll(childSelector).forEach((el) => {
        el.style.width = null
        el.style.display = null
      })
    })
  }

  // these functions allow automatic linebreaks to function better in dynamic width content
  // such as table cells or learnosity rendered content
  MathJax.Hub.Register.MessageHook("Begin PreProcess", function (message) {
    const tables = Array.from(message[1].querySelectorAll('table'));
    if (message[1].nodeName === 'TABLE') {
      tables.push(message[1])
    }
    tables.forEach((table) => {
      const cells = table.querySelectorAll('td,th');
      cells.forEach((cell) => {
        if (cell.querySelector('.math-tex')) {
          cell.appendChild(buildMathJaxPlaceholder(cell.offsetWidth));
        }
      });
    });
    expandChildren(message[1], '.lrn_math_response', '.lrn_item')
    expandChildren(message[1], '.lrn_qr.lrn_choicematrix .lrn_response_input,.lrn_response', '.lrn-stem-text')
  })

  MathJax.Hub.Register.MessageHook("End Process", function (message) {
    const placeholders = message[1].querySelectorAll('.math-tex-placeholder');
    placeholders.forEach(placeholder => placeholder.remove());
    contractChildren(message[1], '.lrn_math_response', '.lrn_item')
    contractChildren(message[1], '.lrn_qr.lrn_choicematrix .lrn_response_input,.lrn_response', '.lrn-stem-text')
  })

  MathJax.Hub.Config({
    messageStyle: "none",
    showMathMenu: true,

  <script>
    window.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
      window.addEventListener('message', ({ origin, data }) => {
        const isSameDomain = (origin === "https://ilclassroom.com")
        if (isSameDomain && typeof data === 'object' && data.message === 'authenticated') {
          const form = document.getElementById('clever-auth-check-form')
          if (form) {
            form.action = data.url
            const input = document.getElementById('clever-auth-check-auth-token')
            if (input) {
              input.value = document.head.querySelector('[name=csrf-token]')['content']
              form.submit()
            }
          }
        }
      })
    })
  </script>

</svg><!----><!----><!----></div><div class="flex w-3/4 flex-col gap-y-4 lg:w-1/2"><h1 id="resource-name" itemprop="name" class="m-0 flex flex-grow text-white">Alg1.5: Introduction to Exponential Functions</h1><div class="mt-2"><span class="bg-primary-200 rounded px-3 py-1 text-sm">Customized by New York City Department of Education</span></div><p itemprop="description" class="leading-normal text-white">Approximately 24 days. In this unit, students are introduced to exponential relationships. Students learn that exponential relationships are characterized by a constant quotient over equal intervals, and compare them to linear relationships which are characterized by a constant difference over equal intervals.</p></div><div class="flex flex-row space-x-2"><div class="page-head__actions flex items-center space-x-3 self-start"><!----><!----></div></div></div></div></div><div class="page-head-nav mt-8"><div class="mx-auto max-w-7xl px-3 md:px-6"><div role="tablist" class="lzui-nav-tabs vue-tabs"><button role="tab" aria-selected="true" type="button" class="text-sm active">Wiki</button><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" type="button" class="text-sm">Included in</button></div></div></div><div id="resource-content" class="active page-content border-none" style="display: block;"><div class="grid max-w-7xl grid-cols-12 px-3 gap-x-3 md:px-6 md:gap-x-6 mx-auto" id=""><div class="col-span-12 break-words py-4"><section class="space-y-6"><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><h2>Unit Overview</h2></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><hr></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>In this unit, students are introduced to exponential relationships. Students learn that exponential relationships are characterized by a constant quotient over equal intervals, and compare them&nbsp;to linear relationships which are characterized by a constant difference over equal intervals. They encounter contexts with quantities that change exponentially. These contexts are presented verbally and with tables and graphs. They construct equations and use them to model situations and solve problems. They learn that the output of an increasing exponential function is eventually greater than the output of an increasing linear function for the same input.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>Students view these new types of relationships as functions and employ the notation and terminology of functions (for example, dependent and independent variables). They study graphs of exponential functions both in terms of contexts they represent and abstract functions that don't represent a particular context, observing the effect of different values of&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>a</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" style="width: 0.503em; vertical-align: -0.309em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.128em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">f(x)=ab^x</script></span>.&nbsp; The context of credit (both in terms of loans and savings) is used through several lessons.</p></div><div class="closed section-accordion bg-focus border-neutral-300 relative mb-4 mt-3 rounded-2xl border shadow-sm"><button class="hover:text-important-hover group m-0 flex w-full cursor-pointer items-center gap-2 rounded-2xl px-4 py-5 text-xl font-bold" aria-expanded="false"><div class="group-hover:bg-base flex h-10 w-10 items-center justify-center rounded-xl transition-colors duration-300"><svg aria-hidden="true" class="text-accent inline-block h-6 w-6 transform transition" stroke="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" id="root-2148252a-797a-445f-9235-16b332b4a191">
<path d="M9 5L16 12L9 19" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path>
</svg></div> Unit at-a-glance</button><div class="section-accordion__body space-y-6 rounded-b-2xl px-3 pb-6 md:px-6" style="display: none;"><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><h3><b>Total Lessons: 21</b></h3></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><ul>

	<li>The prompt, "Critically Examining National Debt" can be used after Lesson 17. &nbsp;</li>
</ul></div></div></div><div class="closed section-accordion bg-focus border-neutral-300 relative mb-4 mt-3 rounded-2xl border shadow-sm"><button class="hover:text-important-hover group m-0 flex w-full cursor-pointer items-center gap-2 rounded-2xl px-4 py-5 text-xl font-bold" aria-expanded="false"><div class="group-hover:bg-base flex h-10 w-10 items-center justify-center rounded-xl transition-colors duration-300"><svg aria-hidden="true" class="text-accent inline-block h-6 w-6 transform transition" stroke="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" id="root-e998d01f-fd23-4f00-87ca-290461477d4a">
<path d="M9 5L16 12L9 19" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path>
</svg></div> Learning goals</button><div class="section-accordion__body space-y-6 rounded-b-2xl px-3 pb-6 md:px-6" style="display: none;"><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>The teacher-facing learning goals below summarize, in teacher language, the mathematical, pedagogical, and language goals of each lesson.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><table style="width:100%;">
	<thead>
		<tr>
			<th>Section</th>
			<th>Teacher-facing learning goals</th>
		</tr>
	</thead>
	<tbody>
		<tr>
			<td><b>Looking at Growth</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 1</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Compare linear and exponential relationships by performing calculations and by interpreting graphs that show two growth patterns.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 2</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Describe (using words and expressions) patterns in tables that represent linear and exponential relationships.</li>
				<li>Given descriptions of linear and exponential relationships, create tables of values and write expressions.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>
		</tr>
		<tr>
			<td><b>A New Kind of Relationship</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 3</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Explain (in writing) how to see&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>a</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="width: 0.503em; 				<li>Interpret&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>a</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="width: 0.503em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.066em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1004.07em, 2.753em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.253em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; 				<li>Write an equation of the form of&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><mo>&amp;#x22C5;</mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="width: 4.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.066em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1004.07em, 2.753em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-52"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-53" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.253em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.253em;">a</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.253em;"></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="padding-left: 0.253em;"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.372em; left: 0.441em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><mo></mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">y=a \cdot b^x</script></span>&nbsp;to represent a quantity&nbsp;&nbsp;that changes by a growth factor&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>b</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="width: 0.441em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.441em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1000.44em, 2.566em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-62" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.816em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>b</mi></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">b</script></span>.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 4</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Comprehend that the term "exponential growth" describes a quantity that changes by a growth factor that is greater than 1, and the term exponential decay describes a quantity that changes by a growth factor that is less than 1 but greater than 0.</li>
				<li>Use only multiplication to represent decreasing a quantity by some fraction of itself.</li>
				<li>Write an expression or an equation to represent a situation where a quantity decays exponentially.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 5</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Calculate growth factor using points on a graph that represents exponential decay.</li>
				<li>Graph equations that represent quantities that change by a growth factor between 0 and 1.</li>
				<li>Interpret equations and graphs that represent exponential decay situations.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 6</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Determine whether situations are characterized by exponential growth or by exponential decay given descriptions and graphs.</li>
				<li>Use graphs to compare and contrast situations that involve exponential decay.</li>
				<li>Use information from a graph to write an equation that represents exponential decay.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 7</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Interpret a negative exponent in equations that represent exponential growth or decay.</li>
				<li>Write and graph an equation that represents exponential decay to solve problems.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>
		</tr>
		<tr>
			<td><b>Exponential Functions</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 8</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Determine and explain (orally and in writing) whether relationshipsin descriptions, tables, equations, or graphsare functions.</li>
				<li>Use function notation to write equations that represent exponential relationships.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 9</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Determine whether a graph that represents a situation should be continuous or discrete.</li>
				<li>Interpret graphs of exponential functions and equations written in function notation to answer questions about a context.</li>
				<li>Use function notation to describe an exponential relationship represented by a graph.</li>
				<li>Use graphing technology to graph exponential functions and analyze their domains.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 10</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Calculate the average rate of change of a function over a specified interval.</li>
				<li>Explain (in writing) how well given rates of change reflect the changes in an exponential function.</li>
				<li>Understand that an exponential function, unlike a linear function, has different average rate of change values for different intervals.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 11</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Choose an appropriate model for a situation when given data.</li>
				<li>Determine graphing windows that would make a graph more informative or meaningful.</li>
				<li>Use exponential functions to model situations that involve exponential growth or decay.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 12</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Describe (orally and in writing) the effect of changing&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>a</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="width: 0.503em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.503em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.753em, 1000.5em, 2.566em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-66"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.566em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>a</mi></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">a</script></span>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>b</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-68" style="width: 0.441em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.441em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1000.44em, 2.566em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; 				<li>Use equations and graphs to compare exponential functions.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 13</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Identify the initial value and growth factor of an exponential function given a graph showing two points with non-consecutive input values.</li>
				<li>Interpret the intersection of the graphs of two functions that represent a situation.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>
		</tr>
		<tr>
			<td><b>Percent Growth and Decay</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 14 - Optional</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Given a starting amount and a percent increase or decrease, calculate a final amount.</li>
				<li>Write expressions using only multiplication to represent a percent increase or decrease.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 15</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Calculate the result of applying a percent increase repeatedly and write the result as a numerical value and expression.</li>

			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 16</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Compare the outcome of applying a percent increase,&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>p</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="width: 0.503em; 			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 17</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Calculate the result of repeated percent increase for the same initial balance and interest rate, but compounded at different intervals.</li>
				<li>Compare interest rates and compounding intervals to choose the better investment option.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 18</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Interpret and evaluate exponential expressions to solve problems.</li>
				<li>Write equivalent expressions to highlight different aspects of a situation that involves repeated percent increase or decrease.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>
		</tr>
		<tr>
			<td><b>Comparing Linear and Exponential Functions</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 19</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Use graphs and calculations to show that a quantity that increases exponentially will eventually surpass one that increases linearly.</li>
				<li>Use tables, calculations, and graphs to compare growth rates of linear and exponential functions.</li>
			</ul>

			<p><b>Lesson 20</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Calculate rates of change of functions given graphs, equations, or tables.</li>
				<li>Use rates of change and show that, for any equal intervals of the independent variable, an exponential function always increases or decreases by an equal factor.</li>
				<li>Use rates of change to show that, for any equal intervals of the independent variable, a linear function always changes by an equal difference.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>
		</tr>
		<tr>
			<td><b>Putting It All Together</b></td>
			<td>
			<p><b>Lesson 21</b></p>

			<ul>
				<li>Choose and write a linear or exponential function to model real-world data.</li>
				<li>Determine and explain (in writing) how well a function models the given data.</li>
				<li>Use given population data to calculate or estimate growth rates and make predictions.</li>
			</ul>
			</td>

<path d="M9 5L16 12L9 19" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path>
</svg></div> Full unit narrative</button><div class="section-accordion__body space-y-6 rounded-b-2xl px-3 pb-6 md:px-6" style="display: none;"><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>Before starting this unit, students are familiar with linear functions from previous units in this course and from work in grade 8. They have been formally introduced to functions and function notation and have explored the behaviors and traits of both linear and non-linear functions. Additionally, students have spent significant time graphing, interpreting graphs, and exploring how to compare the graphs of two linear functions to each other. In this unit, students frequently use the properties of exponents, a topic developed in grade 8. They also apply their understanding of percent change from grade 7 and use an exponent to express repeated increase or decrease by the same percentage.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>In this unit, students are introduced to exponential relationships. Students learn that exponential relationships are characterized by a constant quotient over equal intervals, and compare it to linear relationships which are characterized by a constant difference over equal intervals. They encounter contexts that change exponentially. These contexts are presented verbally and with tables and graphs. They construct equations and use them to model situations and solve problems. Students investigate these exponential relationships without using function notation and language so that they can focus on gaining an appreciation for critical&nbsp;properties and characteristics of exponential relationships.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>Students subsequently view these new types of relationships as functions and employ the notation and terminology of functions (for example, dependent and independent variables). They study graphs of exponential functions both in terms of contexts they represent and abstract functions that dont represent a particular context, observing the effect of different values of&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>a</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" style="width: 0.503em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.503em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.753em, 1000.5em, 2.566em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.566em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>a</mi></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">a</script></span>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>b</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="width: 0.441em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.441em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1000.44em, 2.566em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-124" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.059em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.816em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>b</mi></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">b</script></span>&nbsp;on the graph of the function&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>f</mi></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-125" style="width: 0.566em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.566em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.503em, 1000.57em, 2.753em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.066em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.066em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>f</mi></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">f</script></span>&nbsp;represented by&nbsp;<span class="math-tex"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0" data-mathml="<math xmlns=&quot;http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML&quot;><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy=&quot;false&quot;>(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy=&quot;false&quot;>)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math>" role="presentation" style="position: relative;"><nobr aria-hidden="true"><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="width: 4.691em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.691em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.441em, 1004.69em, 2.816em, -999.997em); top: -2.372em; left: 0em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-129"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-130" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.066em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-131" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-132" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-133" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.253em;">=</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.253em;">a</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.941em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.128em, 1000.44em, 4.191em, -999.997em); top: -3.997em; left: 0em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.372em; left: 0.441em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.309em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.128em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>f</mi><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">f(x)=ab^x</script></span>.&nbsp;</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>The context of credit (both in terms of loans and savings) is used through several lessons to:</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><ul>
	<li>contextualize a percent change applied repeatedly</li>
	<li>make a distinction between (for example) applying 10% increase followed by another 10% increase versus applying a 20% increase to the original amount</li>
	<li>strategically write and interpret expressions and relate them back to a context</li>
	<li>write equivalent expressions in a different way to highlight a different aspect of the situation</li>
</ul></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>In this unit, students learn that the output of an increasing exponential function is eventually greater than the output of an increasing linear function for the same input. In a later unit, students are introduced to quadratic functions. At that time, students will also extend their understanding of exponential functions by how they relate to quadratic functions, understanding that an exponential growth function will eventually exceed both a linear and a quadratic function.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>The contexts used earlier in this unit lead to functions where the domain is the integers. Later, students encounter functions where the domain&nbsp;includes the real numbers. Students do not yet know how to manipulate exponential expressions where the exponents are not whole numbers, but they can interpret the meaning of fractional values in the domain and use a graph to approximate corresponding values in the range.</p></div><div class="ck-editable clear-both"><p>Note on materials: Students should have access to a calculator with an exponent button throughout the unit. Access to graphing technology is necessary for some activities, starting in lesson 7. Examples of graphing technology include a handheld graphing calculator, a computer with a graphing calculator application installed, or an internet-enabled device with access to a site like desmos.com/calculator or geogebra.org/graphing. Interactive applets are embedded throughout, and a graphing calculator tool is accessible in the Math Tools in the digital version.</p></div></div></div><div class="closed section-accordion bg-focus border-neutral-300 relative mb-4 mt-3 rounded-2xl border shadow-sm"><button class="hover:text-important-hover group m-0 flex w-full cursor-pointer items-center gap-2 rounded-2xl px-4 py-5 text-xl font-bold" aria-expanded="false"><div class="group-hover:bg-base flex h-10 w-10 items-center justify-center rounded-xl transition-colors duration-300"><svg aria-hidden="true" class="text-accent inline-block h-6 w-6 transform transition" stroke="currentColor" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" id="root-cc9bac63-8eb3-4662-88ef-cfbfabad227b">
<path d="M9 5L16 12L9 19" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"></path>

width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.372em; left: 0.441em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.378em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.247em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.003em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><mi>y</mi><mo>=</mo><mi>a</mi><mo></mo><msup><mi>b</mi><mi>x</mi></msup></math></span></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">y=a \cdot b^x</script></span>. (Lesson 5)</li>
	<li>I can find a growth factor from a graph and write an equation to represent exponential decay. (Lesson 5)</li>
	<li>I can graph equations that represent quantities that change by a growth factor between 0 and 1. (Lesson 5)</li>
	<li>I can use graphs to compare and contrast situations that involve exponential decay. (Lesson 6)</li>
	<li>I can use information from a graph to write an equation that represents exponential decay. (Lesson 6)</li>
	<li>I can describe the meaning of a negative exponent in equations that represent exponential decay. (Lesson 7)</li>
	<li>I can write and graph an equation that represents exponential decay to solve problems. (Lesson 7)</li>

	<li>I can use function notation to write equations that represent exponential relationships. (Lesson 8)</li>
	<li>When I see relationships in descriptions, tables, equations, or graphs, I can determine whether the relationships are functions. (Lesson 8)</li>
	<li>I can analyze a situation and determine whether it makes sense to connect the points on the graph that represents the situation. (Lesson 9)</li>
	<li>When I see a graph of an exponential function, I can make sense of and describe the relationship using function notation. (Lesson 9)</li>
	<li>I can calculate the average rate of change of a function over a specified period of time. (Lesson 10)</li>
	<li>I know how the average rate of change of an exponential function differs from that of a linear function. (Lesson 10)</li>
	<li>I can use exponential functions to model situations that involve exponential growth or decay. (Lesson 11)</li>
	<li>When given data, I can determine an appropriate model for the situation described by the data. (Lesson 11)</li>
